title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/hw/: \'wh\' in \'why\'">hw</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: \'a\' in \'father\'">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:\xc2\xa0</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[sa\xc5\x8b \xcb\x88xwan]</a></span>, <i>Saint <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John</a></i>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and most populous <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. insular area)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States#Unincorporated_organized_territories" title="Territories of the United States">unincorporated territory</a> of the United States. As of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">2010 census</a>, it had a population of 395,326 making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">46th-largest</a> city under the jurisdiction of the United States. San Juan was founded by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> colonists in 1521, who called it <i>Ciudad de Puerto Rico</i> ("Rich Port City"). Puerto Rico\'s capital is the second oldest European-established capital city in the Americas, after <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SJCOPRI_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-SJCOPRI-5">[5]</a></sup> Several historical buildings are located in San Juan; among the most notable are the city\'s former defensive forts, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Fort San Felipe del Morro">Fort San Felipe del Morro</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_San_Crist%C3%B3bal" title="Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal">Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, the oldest executive mansion in continuous use in the Americas.</p>\n<p>Today, San Juan is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Juan_Port" title="San Juan Port">Puerto Rico\'s most important seaport</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and is the island\'s manufacturing,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> financial, cultural, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Tourism in Puerto Rico">tourism center</a>. The population of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo metropolitan area">Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>, including San Juan and the municipalities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayamon,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayamon, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canovanas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Canovanas, Puerto Rico">Can\xc3\xb3vanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Alta, Puerto Rico">Toa Alta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>, is about 2\xc2\xa0million inhabitants; thus, about half the population of Puerto Rico now lives and works in this area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> San Juan is also a principal city of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_metropolitan_area#Combined_Statistical_Area" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan-Caguas-Fajardo Combined Statistical Area</a>. The city has been the host of events within the sports community, including the 1979 <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>, 1966 <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a>, events of the 2006, 2009 and 2013 <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLB" title="MLB">MLB</a> San Juan Series in 2010.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span flag of San Juan</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Government"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Colleges_and_universities"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Colleges and universities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Public_and_private_schools"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Public and private schools</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Public transport</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Health_and_utilities"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Health and utilities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Professional_teams"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">Professional cities</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Notable_people_from_San_Juan"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Notable people from San Juan</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Timeline of San Juan, Puerto Rico">Timeline of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="768" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG/200px-Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG/300px-Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG/400px-Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nRuins of Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n\'s residence at Caparra</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1508, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a> founded the original settlement which he called <a href="/wiki/Caparra_Archaeological_Site" title="Caparra Archaeological Site">Caparra</a>. It was named after the Province of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caceres_(province)" title="Caceres (province)">Caceres</a> in Spain, the birthplace of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_de_Ovando" title="Nicol\xc3\xa1s de Ovando">Nicol\xc3\xa1s de Ovando</a>, then the Governor of Spain\'s Caribbean territories,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Today it is part of the Pueblo Viejo sector of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaynabo" title="Guaynabo">Guaynabo</a>, just to the west of the present San Juan metropolitan area. A year later, the settlement was moved to a site then called Puerto Rico, Spanish for "rich port" or "good port", after its similar geographical features to the town of Puerto Rico of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caparra_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caparra-9">[9]</a></sup> In 1521, the newer settlement was given its formal name, <i>Puerto Rico de San Juan Bautista</i>.</p>\n<p>The ambiguous use of <i>San Juan Bautista</i> and <i>Puerto Rico</i> for both the city and the island in time led to a reversal in practical use by most inhabitants: by 1746 the name for the city (Puerto Rico) had become that of the entire island, leading to the city being identified as <i>Puerto Rico de Puerto Rico</i> on maps of the era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistoryS.J._11-0"><a href="#cite_note-HistoryS.J.-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Staat_van_Amerika,_map_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico,_1766.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="750" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg/250px-Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg/375px-Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg/500px-Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Staat_van_Amerika,_map_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico,_1766.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSan Juan and bay, Puerto Rico, 1766</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>San Juan, as a settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, was used by merchant and military ships traveling from Spain as the first stopover in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>. Because of its prominence in the Caribbean, a network of fortifications was built to protect the transports of gold and silver from the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> to Europe. Because of the rich cargoes, San Juan became a target of the foreign powers of the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The city was witness to attacks from the English led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Francis_Drake" title="Sir Francis Drake">Sir Francis Drake</a> in 1595 (in what is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Battle of Puerto Rico">Battle of Puerto Rico</a>) and by <a href="/wiki/George_Clifford,_3rd_Earl_of_Cumberland" title="George Clifford, 3rd Earl of Cumberland">George Clifford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Cumberland" title="Earl of Cumberland">Earl of Cumberland</a>, in 1598. Artillery from San Juan\'s fort, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Fort San Felipe del Morro">El Morro</a>, repelled Drake; however, Clifford managed to land troops and lay siege to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-14">[14]</a></sup> After a few months of English occupation, Clifford was forced to abandon the siege when his troops began to suffer from exhaustion and sickness. In 1625 the city was sacked by Dutch forces led by Captain Balduino Enrico (also known as Boudewijn Hendricksz/Bowdoin Henrick), but El Morro withstood the assault and was not taken. The Dutch were counterattacked by Captain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan_de_Amezquita" title="Juan de Amezquita">Juan de Amezquita</a> and 50 members of the civilian militia on land and by the cannons of the Spanish troops in El Morro Castle. The land battle left 60 Dutch soldiers dead and Enrico with a sword wound to his neck which he received from the hands of Amezquita.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (January 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> The Dutch ships at sea were boarded by Puerto Ricans who defeated those aboard. After a long battle, the Spanish soldiers and volunteers of the city\'s militia were able to defend the city from the attack and save the island from an invasion. On October 21, Enrico set La Fortaleza and the city ablaze. Captains Amezquita and Andre Botello decided to put a stop to the destruction and led 200 men in an attack against the enemy\'s front and rear guard. They drove Enrico and his men from their trenches and into the ocean in their haste to reach their ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRH_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRH-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Juan_(1797)" title="Battle of San Juan (1797)">attack</a> in 1797, during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">Sir Ralph Abercromby</a> (who had just conquered <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>). His army laid siege to the city but was forced to withdraw in defeat as the Puerto Rican defenses proved more resilient than those of Trinidad. Various events and circumstances, including liberalized commerce with Spain, the opening of the island to immigrants as a direct result of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Decree_of_Graces_of_1815" title="Royal Decree of Graces of 1815">Royal Decree of Graces of 1815</a>, and the colonial revolutions, led to an expansion of San Juan and other Puerto Rican settlements in the late 18th and early 19th century.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Photographic_Company_(0766).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1204" data-file-width="1536" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg/220px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg/330px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg/440px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Photographic_Company_(0766).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nLa Plaza, San Juan, ca. 1900</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On May 8, 1898, United States Navy ships, among them the <a href="/wiki/USS_Detroit_(C-10)" title="USS Detroit (C-10)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Detroit</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Indiana_(BB-1)" title="USS Indiana (BB-1)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Indiana</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_New_York_(ACR-2)" title="USS New York (ACR-2)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>New York</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Amphitrite_(BM-2)" title="USS Amphitrite (BM-2)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Amphitrite</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Terror_(BM-4)" title="USS Terror (BM-4)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Terror</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Montgomery_(C-9)" title="USS Montgomery (C-9)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Montgomery</i></a>, commanded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rear_Admiral_(United_States)" title="Rear Admiral (United States)">Rear Admiral</a> <a href="/wiki/William_T._Sampson" title="William T. Sampson">William T. Sampson</a> arrived at San Juan Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The USS <i>Yale</i> captured a Spanish freighter, the <i>Rita</i> in San Juan Bay, thus being the first hostile encounter between the warring sides in Puerto Rico. On May 9, <i>Yale</i> fought a brief battle with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auxiliary_cruiser" title="Auxiliary cruiser">auxiliary cruiser</a> of Spain, name unknown, resulting in a Spanish victory. Around this time, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Rivero_M%C3%A9ndez" title="\xc3\x81ngel Rivero M\xc3\xa9ndez">Captain \xc3\x81ngel Rivero M\xc3\xa9ndez</a> was assigned the command of the Spanish forces in the fortress of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (Puerto Rico)">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a> in San Juan. On May 10, the <i>Yale</i> returned to San Juan Bay, Rivero-M\xc3\xa9ndez ordered his men to open fire upon the <a href="/wiki/USS_Yale_(1888)" title="USS Yale (1888)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Yale</i></a> using an Ordo\xc3\xb1ez 15 centimeter cannon, thus becoming the first attack against the Americans in Puerto Rico during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHA_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-GHA-19">[19]</a></sup> For his actions, Captain Rivero-Mendez was awarded the "Cruz de la Orden de Merito Militar" (The Cross of the Order of the Military Merit) first class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHA_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-GHA-19">[19]</a></sup> The residents of San Juan were furious with Rivero and blamed him for the destruction caused to their city by the American bombardments. Nothing came of those accusations and Capt. Rivero-M\xc3\xa9ndez was ordered to turn over the keys of all the military installations in San Juan to Captain Henry A. Reed of the U.S. Army after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> was signed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHA_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-GHA-19">[19]</a></sup> On July 25, General <a href="/wiki/Nelson_A._Miles" title="Nelson A. Miles">Nelson A. Miles</a> landed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a> (in southwestern Puerto Rico) with 3,300\xc2\xa0soldiers in what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Campaign" title="Puerto Rican Campaign">Puerto Rican Campaign</a>. The American troops found some resistance and engaged the Spanish and Puerto Rican troops in battle, the most notable of these the battles of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yauco" title="Battle of Yauco">Yauco</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Asomante" title="Battle of Asomante">Asomante</a>. All military actions in Puerto Rico were suspended August 13, 1898, after President <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a> and French Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Jules_Cambon" title="Jules Cambon">Jules Cambon</a>, acting on behalf of the Spanish government, signed an <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">armistice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COPRSAW_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-COPRSAW-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Spain ceded the island to the United States later the same year by signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Camp_Las_Casas" title="Camp Las Casas">Camp Las Casas</a>, located in the district of Santurce, served as the main training camp for the Puerto Rican soldiers prior to World War I and World War II; the majority of the men trained in this facility were assigned to the "Porto Rico Regiment of Infantry" which was renamed the <a href="/wiki/65th_Infantry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="65th Infantry Regiment (United States)">65th Infantry Regiment</a> of the United States Army by the Reorganization Act of June 4, 1920. The 65th Infantry was deactivated in 1956 and became the only unit ever to be transferred from an active Army component to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico National Guard">Puerto Rico National Guard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRR_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-PRR-22">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2024" data-file-width="3000" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg/220px-MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg/330px-MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg/440px-MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MODERN_BUILDINGS_TOWER_OVER_THE_SHANTIES_CROWDED_ALONG_THE_MARTIN_PENA_CANAL_-_NARA_-_546369.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nShanty town along the Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Canal, 1973</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Marxuach" title="Te\xc3\xb3filo Marxuach">Te\xc3\xb3filo Marxuach</a> (Retired as a Lieutenant Colonel), a native of <a href="/wiki/Arroyo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arroyo, Puerto Rico">Arroyo, Puerto Rico</a>, fired the first shot in what is considered to be the first shot of World War I fired by the regular armed forces of the United States against any ship flying the colors of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNI_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-USNI-23">[23]</a></sup> Marxuach, who was a member of the "Porto Rico Regiment of Infantry" and Officer of the Day, on March 25, 1915, opened fire on the <i>Odenwald</i>, an armed German supply vessel, when it was trying to force its way out of San Juan\'s bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-24">[24]</a></sup> The shots ordered by Lt. Marxuach were the first fired by the United States in World War I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1919, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Rigau_Carrera" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Rigau Carrera">F\xc3\xa9lix Rigau Carrera</a>, "El Aguila de Sabana Grande" (The Eagle from Sabana Grande), the first Puerto Rican pilot, became the first native Puerto Rican to fly an aircraft in the island when he flew his <a href="/wiki/Curtiss_JN-4" title="Curtiss JN-4">Curtiss JN-4</a> from Las Casas. At the time, the area was used by the military as an air base and it was also Puerto Rico\'s first commercial airport, and Rigau Carrera was allowed to perform his historic flight from the air field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EM_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-EM-26">[26]</a></sup> Camp Las Casas was eventually closed down, and in 1950 a public housing project by the name of <a href="/wiki/Residencial_Las_Casas" title="Residencial Las Casas">Residencial Fray Bartolome de Las Casas</a> was constructed on its former location.</p>\n<p>On January 2, 1947, the people of San Juan elected <a href="/wiki/Felisa_Rinc%C3%B3n_de_Gautier" title="Felisa Rinc\xc3\xb3n de Gautier">Felisa Rinc\xc3\xb3n de Gautier</a> (also known as Do\xc3\xb1a Fela) (1897\xe2\x80\x931994) as their mayor. Thus, she became the first woman to be elected as the mayor of a capital city in any of The Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> era, she ordered the establishment of the island\'s first Civil Defense system under the directorship of Colonel <a href="/wiki/Gilberto_Jos%C3%A9_Marxuach" title="Gilberto Jos\xc3\xa9 Marxuach">Gilberto Jos\xc3\xa9 Marxuach</a> (Te\xc3\xb3filo\'s son).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Rinc\xc3\xb3n de Gautier served as mayor until January 2, 1969.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_(Puerto_Rico)-Spanish_Rule.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="451" data-file-width="298" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg/160px-Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg/240px-Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg/320px-Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg.png 2x" width="160"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_(Puerto_Rico)-Spanish_Rule.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHistoric coat of arms of San Juan (Spanish rule)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On October 30, 1950, San Juan was the scene of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Juan_Uprising" title="San Juan Uprising">San Juan Uprising</a>, one of many uprisings which occurred in various towns and cities in Puerto Rico, by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nationalist_Party" title="Puerto Rican Nationalist Party">Puerto Rican Nationalist Party</a> against the governments of Puerto Rico and the United States. Among the uprising\'s main objective was to attack "<a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>" (the Governors mansion) and the United States Federal Court House Building in <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>. In accordance to the planned uprising in San Juan, a group of nationalists were supposed to attack simultaneously the gubernatorial mansion <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, where Puerto Rican governor <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn</a> resided, and the United States Federal Court House which is located close to an area called "La Marina" in Old San Juan. The La Fortaleza battle, which ensued between the nationalists and the police lasted 15 minutes, and ended when four of the five attackers were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Page_2_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Page_2-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms_and_flag_of_San_Juan">Coat of arms and flag of San Juan</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Torres_Vargas" title="Diego de Torres Vargas">Diego de Torres Vargas</a></div>\n<p>On March 8, 1948 the city government of San Juan officially adopted as the city\'s first flag an orange field, in the center of which is the Coat of Arms of the City. The orange color was based and taken from Father <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Torres_Vargas" title="Diego de Torres Vargas">Diego de Torres Vargas</a>\' text and it reads\xc2\xa0: "Escudo de armas dado a Puerto Rico por los Reyes Cat\xc3\xb3licos en el a\xc3\xb1o de 1511, siendo Procurador un vecino llamado Pedro Moreno. Son\xc2\xa0: un cordero blanco con su banderilla colorada, sobre un libro, y todo sobre una isla verde, que es la de Puerto Rico, y por los lados una F y una I, que quiere decir Fernando e Isabel, los Reyes Cat\xc3\xb3licos que se las dieron, y hoy se conservan en el estandarte real, que es de damasco anaranjado, con que se gan\xc3\xb3 la ciudad" ("Coat of Arms given to Puerto Rico by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a> in the year 1511 being Procurator a <a href="/wiki/Vecino" title="Vecino">vecino</a> named Pedro Moreno. They are: a white lamb with a red flag, on top of a book, and everything above a green island, which is Puerto Rico...which is of orange damask, with which the city was won"). It appears that the color was changed from orange to white at some point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">\n<div style="width: 235px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;">\n<div style="margin:31px auto;"><a class="image" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Coat of arms of San Juan</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:151px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_juan_pr.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4096" data-file-width="4096" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/San_juan_pr.jpg/149px-San_juan_pr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/San_juan_pr.jpg/224px-San_juan_pr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/San_juan_pr.jpg/298px-San_juan_pr.jpg 2x" width="149"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_juan_pr.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSan Juan from space</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>San Juan is located along the north-eastern coast of Puerto Rico. It lies south of the Atlantic Ocean; north of <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>; east of and <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. The city occupies an area of 76.93 square miles (199.2\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>), of which, 29.11 square miles (75.4\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>) (37.83%) is water. San Juan\'s main water bodies are <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Bay" title="San Juan Bay">San Juan Bay</a> and two natural lagoons, the <a href="/wiki/Condado_Lagoon" title="Condado Lagoon">Condado</a> and San Jos\xc3\xa9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<p>San Juan has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> and enjoys an average temperature of 81.0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (27.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) although 90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) or higher temperatures are seen on an average 79 days annually, more commonly occurring during the wetter months of the northern summer, especially if the winds come from the south. In the winter, temperatures can drop to around 60\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C), though the average winter low is 71\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (22\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). The coolest temperature officially recorded was 60\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (16\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on March 3, 1957, and the hottest was 98\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (37\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on October 9, 1981;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWC-32">[32]</a></sup> the record cold daily maximum is 71\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (22\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on February 4, 1935, while the record warm daily minimum is 83\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (28\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on August 11, 1995, the most recent of four occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOWData_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-33">[33]</a></sup> Rainfall is well-distributed throughout the year, but the months of January, February, and March are the driest; as March averages just 1.95 inches (49.5\xc2\xa0mm) of rain, the city falls under the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon</a> category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Rainfall averages 56.35 inches (1,431.3\xc2\xa0mm), falling on an average 198.5 days per year;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOWData_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-33">[33]</a></sup> despite this dampness, the city averages 2,970 hours of sunshine per year, or just over \xe2\x85\x94 of the possible total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAAsun_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAAsun-35">[35]</a></sup> Annual rainfall has historically ranged from 35.53\xc2\xa0in (902\xc2\xa0mm) in 1991 to 89.50\xc2\xa0in (2,273\xc2\xa0mm) in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOWData_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-33">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p><br/></p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for <a class="mw-redirect" class="thumbinner">\n<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow: auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan,_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2787" data-file-width="7927" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg/712px-General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg/1067px-General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg/1423px-General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg 2x" width="712"/></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan,_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg" title="File:General view of harbor at San Juan, Porto Rico looking South.jpg"></a></div>\n<center>General view of harbor at San Juan, Puerto Rico looking South to San Juan Bay, 1927. The clock tower building at center was the San Juan Rail Terminal.</center>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1235" data-file-width="1932" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Puerto_Rico_01.jpg/220px-Puerto_Rico_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Puerto_Rico_01.jpg/330px-Puerto_Rico_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Puerto_Rico_01.jpg/440px-Puerto_Rico_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nOld San Juan</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The architecture of San Juan is very diverse, due to its size and all the cultural influences received during its existence. The oldest part of the city, known as <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>, mostly features the influence of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_architecture" title="Spanish architecture">Spanish architecture</a>. This part of the city is comprised by a network of <a href="/wiki/Sett_(paving)" title="Sett (paving)">"setted" roads</a> usually surrounded by ancient, two-storied houses built on <a href="/wiki/Masonry" title="Masonry">masonry</a>. Some colonial structures have been restored and serve either as government offices or museums. Some examples are the <a href="/wiki/Ballaj%C3%A1_Barracks" title="Ballaj\xc3\xa1 Barracks">Ballaj\xc3\xa1 Barracks</a>, which now serve as museum and headquarter of several cultural organizations; <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, which has served as the residence of the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">Governor of Puerto Rico</a> since the 16th Century; and the Ancient Welfare Asylum, which now houses the Institute of Puerto Rican Culture, among others. Old San Juan also features several public squares, like the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Armas,_San_Juan" title="Plaza de Armas, San Juan">Plaza de Armas</a>, located in front of San Juan City Hall; and cathedrals, like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_San_Juan_Bautista" title="Cathedral of San Juan Bautista">Cathedral of San Juan Bautista</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Old San Juan is also notable for being partly enclosed by massive walls and fortifications built by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_government" title="Spanish government">Spanish government</a>.</p>\n<p>The architecture is more varied in other districts of the city. The district of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santurce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a> features a lot of influence from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_deco" title="Art deco">art deco</a>, while the districts of <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hato Rey, Puerto Rico">Hato Rey</a> feature more modern structures.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="1628" height="401" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg/400px-Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg/600px-Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg/800px-Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg 2x" width="400"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDistricts of San Juan</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Subdivisions of San Juan, Puerto Rico">Subdivisions of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>What is now known as <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a> occupied the western end of a rocky islet, the <a href="/wiki/Isleta_de_San_Juan" title="Isleta de San Juan">Isleta de San Juan</a>, at the mouth of San Juan Bay. During the 20th century, the main population centers surged well beyond the walls of the old city and onto Puerto Rico\'s main island, and merged with the existing settlements east and south of Old San Juan. With the annexation of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a> in 1951, the municipality of San Juan grew four times its previous size. As a result, the city is now composed of a variety of districts and neighborhoods. San Juan is now subdivided into 18 districts (<a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">barrios</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> 16 of which fall within the former municipality of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>. Eight districts are further subdivided into sectors (sub-barrios), including two districts in the area that covered the original municipality of San Juan. The 18 districts are:</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n<ol>\n<li><a Antiguo">San Juan Antiguo</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Old San Juan, Puerto Rico">Old San Juan</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tortugo,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tortugo, San Juan, Puerto Rico (page does not exist)">Tortugo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Universidad,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Universidad, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Universidad</a></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_San_Juan">Old San Juan</span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Old San Juan, Puerto Rico">Old San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Juan_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="773" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Juan_3.jpg/250px-San_Juan_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Juan_3.jpg/375px-San_Juan_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Juan_3.jpg/500px-San_Juan_3.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Juan_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSome streets in Old San Juan are still paved with blue <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cobblestones" title="Cobblestones">cobblestones</a> from the Spanish colonial era.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>During the Spanish colonial times most of the urban population resided in what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>. This sector is located on the western half of a small island called the <i>Isleta de San Juan</i>, which is connected to the mainland by two bridges and a <a href="/wiki/Causeway" title="Causeway">causeway</a>. The small island, which comprises an area of 47 square miles (120\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>), also hosts the working-class neighborhood of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra" title="Puerta de Tierra">Puerta de Tierra</a> and most of Puerto Rico\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_Departments_of_the_Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Executive Departments of the Government of Puerto Rico">central government</a> buildings, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Capitol" title="Puerto Rico Capitol">Commonwealth\'s Capitol</a>.</p>\n<p>The main central part of the city is characterized by narrow streets made of blue <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">cobblestone</a> and picturesque colonial buildings, some of which date back to the 16th and 17th century. Sections of the old city are surrounded by massive walls and several defensive structures and notable forts. These include the 16th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Fort San Felipe del Morro">Fort San Felipe del Morro</a> and the 17th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_San_Crist%C3%B3bal" title="Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal">Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>, both part of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_National_Historic_Site" title="San Juan National Historic Site">San Juan National Historic Site</a>, and the 16th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Palacio_de_Santa_Catalina" title="El Palacio de Santa Catalina">El Palacio de Santa Catalina</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, which serves as the governor\'s mansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> Other buildings of interest predating the 20th century are the <i>Ayuntamiento or Alcald\xc3\xada</i> (City Hall), the <i>Diputaci\xc3\xb3n Provincial</i> and the <i>Real Intendencia</i> buildings, which currently house the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_State" title="Puerto Rico Department of State">Puerto Rico Department of State</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosa" title="Casa Rosa">Casa Rosa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Church" title="San Jos\xc3\xa9 Church">San Jos\xc3\xa9 Church</a> (1523) and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Hotel_El_Convento" title="Hotel El Convento">Hotel El Convento</a>, the former house of the Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n family known as <a href="/wiki/Casa_Blanca_(San_Juan)" title="Casa Blanca (San Juan)">Casa Blanca</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Tapia" title="Teatro Tapia">Teatro Tapia</a>, the former Spanish barracks (now Museum of Ballaj\xc3\xa1), <i>La Princesa</i> (former municipal jail, now headquartering the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_Magdalena_de_Pazzis_Cemetery" title="Santa Mar\xc3\xada Magdalena de Pazzis Cemetery">Santa Mar\xc3\xada Magdalena de Pazzis Cemetery</a>, located just outside the city walls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_San_Juan_Bautista" title="Cathedral of San Juan Bautista">Cathedral of San Juan Bautista</a> (construction began in the 1520s) is also located in Old San Juan, and contains the tomb of the Spanish explorer and settlement founder <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Old San Juan, also known as the "old city", is the main cultural tourist attraction in Puerto Rico; its bayside is lined by dock slips for large <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a>.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_districts">Other districts</span></h4>\n<p>East of Old San Juan lies the wealthy tourist-oriented neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">Condado</a>, which occupies land that used to be owned by entrepreneur Pablo Ubarri Capetillo, a Spanish railroad developer and Count of San Jos\xc3\xa9 de Santurce under the Spanish colonial period. Beaches such as nearby <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Park_(Santurce)" title="Ocean Park (Santurce)">Ocean Park</a>, popular with swimmers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surfers" title="Surfers">surfers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitesurfers" title="Kitesurfers">kitesurfers</a>, are found all along the district\'s Atlantic coastline which is also the locus of numerous hotels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Near Condado are two separate business districts, <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miramar_(Santurce)" title="Miramar (Santurce)">Miramar</a>. Miramar is mainly a residential area rising south of the Condado Lagoon. It comprises the former <i><a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">barrio</a></i> of Miraflores, as well as drained marshland and landfill over which was built San Juan\'s first airport, the Isla Grande airport, which was renamed <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" title="Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport">Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport</a> in honor of Major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas-Dominicci" title="Fernando Luis Ribas-Dominicci">Fernando Luis Ribas-Dominicci</a> (USAF). Miramar now hosts the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Convention_Center" title="Puerto Rico Convention Center">Puerto Rico Convention Center</a> as well as some of San Juan Harbor\'s cruise ship piers. In 2005 Miramar was designated an historical district of Puerto Rico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Santurce, originally named <i>San Mateo de Cangrejos</i> (Saint Matthew of the Crabs), was a settlement for freed African slaves during the early days of the city. After Pablo Ubarri sought permission to link San Juan with R\xc3\xado Piedras proper via steam tramway in 1878, the time it took to travel between both points were shortened and thereby stimulated the colonization and growth of the district. At the beginning of the twentieth century an electric trolley was installed, the township was split into three parts, and its main settlement, merged with the city, was renamed using the Spanish spelling of <a href="/wiki/Santurtzi" title="Santurtzi">Santurtzi</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a></i> in Basque), Ubarri\'s birthplace in <a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">Vizcaya</a>, Spain. The "Museo de Arte de Puerto Rico" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Museum_of_Art" title="Puerto Rico Museum of Art">Puerto Rico Museum of Art</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> and other important cultural venues are located in Santurce.</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/70/Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg/220px-Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/70/Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg/330px-Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/70/Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg/440px-Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_San_Juan_Street.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nLooking down an Old San Juan street towards the bay</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>South of Santurce is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a>, part of the former municipality of R\xc3\xado Piedras. Hato Rey was grazing ground for cattle owned by the royal government (hence its name, the <i>King\'s Herd</i> in Spanish) as early as the 16th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mini-wall-street_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-mini-wall-street-50">[49]</a></sup> and is now considered the financial center of the island. A section of this district is often referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Milla_de_Oro" title="Milla de Oro">Milla de Oro</a></i> (actually 0.47 miles or 0.76 kilometers long) due in part to the many banks and businesses located there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mini-wall-street_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-mini-wall-street-50">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the southern part of the city is the socially diversified community of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>. Founded in the mid-1850s, R\xc3\xado Piedras was a separate town which hosted sugar cane plantations and the estates of some of San Juan\'s wealthiest inhabitants (as well as their working class staff). The Spanish colonial governors also had their summer home there on land which eventually gave way to the main campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a>. In 1951 the municipalities of San Juan and R\xc3\xado Piedras were merged to redefine San Juan\'s current city limits. Today R\xc3\xado Piedras comprises the largest area of the municipality of San Juan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> and is home to the "Plaza del Mercado" (R\xc3\xado Piedras <a href="/wiki/Marketplace" title="Marketplace">Marketplace</a>), the main campus and the Medical Sciences campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Botanical_Garden" title="San Juan Botanical Garden">San Juan Botanical Garden</a>.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<table class="infobox bordered" style="font-size:88%">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="3">Race \xe2\x80\x93 San Juan, Puerto Rico \xe2\x80\x93 2010 Census<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Race</th>\n<th>Population</th>\n<th>\xc2\xa0% of Total</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a></b></td>\n<td>268,708</td>\n<td>68.0%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Black/African American</b></td>\n<td>73,538</td>\n<td>18.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" title="Alaska Native">Alaska Native</a></b></td>\n<td>3,071</td>\n<td>0.8%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a></b></td>\n<td>1,750</td>\n<td>0.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiians" title="Native Hawaiians">Native Hawaiians</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">Pacific Islander</a></b></td>\n<td>36</td>\n<td>0.0%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Some other race</b></td>\n<td>32,386</td>\n<td>8.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a></b></td>\n<td>15,835</td>\n<td>4.0%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CHART_2_.jpg"><img alt="CHART 2 .jpg" data-file-height="447" data-file-width="314" height="447" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a9/CHART_2_.jpg" width="314"/></a></div>\n<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CHART_3_.jpg"><img alt="CHART 3 .jpg" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="314" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/80/CHART_3_.jpg" width="314"/></a></div>\n<p>San Juan is the largest city in Puerto Rico by population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-poptotal_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-poptotal-53">[52]</a></sup> From 1899 to 1950 the municipality of San Juan excluded the township of R\xc3\xado Piedras. For this reason, population data and land area for the period make reference only to the Antiguo San Juan and Santurce <i>barrios</i>, or subdivisions, of San Juan. The old municipality of R\xc3\xado Piedras constituted the third most populated city of Puerto Rico at the time of its annexation in 1951. Its strategic location south of the capital served as a junction for all the principal ways of transportation of the island and as a geographical entry to San Juan, which are factors that prompted R\xc3\xado Piedras\'s dramatic urban development in the 20th century.</p>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>, the racial composition of San Juan was as follows:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a>: 68.0% (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">Non-Hispanic Whites</a>: 1.2%)</li>\n<li>Black or African American: 18.3% (Non-Hispanic Blacks: 0.3%)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a>: 0.8%</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>: 0.4%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiians" title="Native Hawaiians">Native Hawaiian</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">Pacific Islander</a>: 0.0%</li>\n<li>Some other race: 8.2%</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a>: 4.0%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> (of any race): 98.2%</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Among the Hispanic and Latino population, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Ricans</a> are, unsurprisingly, the largest group; they make up 87.5% of San Juan\'s Hispanic population. People of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">Dominican</a> descent made up 12.2% of the Hispanic population, while those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">Cuban</a> descent formed 1.7% of the Hispanic populace. Other Hispanic and Latino groups collectively formed 3.2% of San Juan\'s Hispanic population.</p>\n<p>There are 13,304 whites of non-Hispanic origin living in San Juan; 10,571 blacks of non-Hispanic origin living in San Juan. Non-Hispanic whites and blacks form 3.2% and 2.6% of San Juan\'s population respectively. There are also approximately 562 Asians of non-Hispanic origin in San Juan; they make up only 0.1% of the population. However, Asians of Hispanic and non-Hispanic origin together number at 6,342. The vast majority of Asians in San Juan are of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_American" title="Chinese American">Chinese</a> descent; of the 6,342 Asians, 4,928 are Chinese. Chinese comprise 1.4% of the population. The only other sizable Asian group in San Juan are <a href="/wiki/Indian_Americans" title="Indian Americans">Indian Americans</a>; there are 698 people of Indian descent in the city, forming 0.2% of the population. There are very small numbers of people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_American" title="Filipino American">Filipino</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_American" title="Japanese American">Japanese</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_American" title="Vietnamese American">Vietnamese</a> ancestry; none of these groups number more than 100 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<p>According to the 2006\xe2\x80\x932008 American Community Survey, 87.5% of San Juan\'s population was native and 12.5% were foreign-born. Of the native population, 86.9% were born in Puerto Rico or the United States, of which 75.6% were born in Puerto Rico and 8.9% were born in the United States. The remaining 0.7% were born in a U.S. territory or were born abroad to American parents. The remaining 11.9% of the population were born outside the United States, Puerto Rico, and U.S. territories. In recent years, an increasing number of Americans not of Hispanic ancestry (both of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> and of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White American</a> descent) have moved to San Juan. In addition, a large number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stateside_Puerto_Ricans" title="Stateside Puerto Ricans">Stateside Puerto Ricans</a> have settled in the city upon their return to Puerto Rico. There is also a growing <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> population, both of Hispanic and non-Hispanic origin.</p>\n<p>In terms of ancestry, 23,875 people claimed American ancestry, which is equivalent to 5.8% of San Juan\'s population. Other sizable ancestry groups included those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> descent, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_American" title="French American">French</a> descent, and <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> descent. People of Italian descent numbered at 1,694, forming 0.4% of the population; people of French descent numbered at 1,064, forming 0.2% of the population. Finally, those of West Indian descent numbered at 1,393, forming 0.3% of San Juan\'s population. Approximately 1,026 people claimed <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> ancestry; 719 claimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> ancestry; 646 claimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a> ancestry; 431 claimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_American" title="Arab American">Arab</a> ancestry, and 346 claimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> ancestry. There are many other ancestry groups in San Juan, but they are very scant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<p>San Juan experienced significant economic growth following World War II. During this period the city underwent an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a>, although as of 1984 it had never generated its own economic region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> The city\'s economy relies mostly on companies dedicated to the manufacture of several products, including: <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">Chemical substances</a> (bleach and house cleaning products); medicines; rum and other beverages; <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a>; electric tools; <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronic devices</a>; plastics, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>, and food-based products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> Tourism is also a key industry, based on San Juan\'s proximity to Puerto Rico\'s main airport, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> The tourism focus of the city is located in the district of Condado Beach where there are luxurious hotels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> Historical locations such as El Morro, Old San Juan and El Cuartel de Ballaja are promoted in tourism campaigns. The district of Hato Rey contains a corporate sector known as "La Milla de Oro", (The Golden Mile) which serves as the headquarters of local and international banks. San Juan\'s Hato Rey district is often referred to as the "Wall Street of the Caribbean", due to the influence of the area on Puerto Rico and the Caribbean\'s economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mini-wall-street_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-mini-wall-street-50">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Seaborne_Airlines" title="Seaborne Airlines">Seaborne Airlines</a> is headquartered on the 9th floor of the World Plaza Building in San Juan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flying_into_San_Juan-Puerto_Rico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSan Juan beach</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Technological advances after World War II in the development of the airliner, coupled with the island\'s climate and natural setting, have transformed San Juan into the springboard for tourism around the island, and has made the rest of the Caribbean known throughout the world during the last fifty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Today the capital features hotels, museums, historical buildings, restaurants, beaches and shopping centers. In San Juan there are tourist attractions, including: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Old San Juan, Puerto Rico">Old San Juan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_Park,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ocean Park, Puerto Rico">Ocean Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isla_Verde,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isla Verde, Puerto Rico">Isla Verde</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Condado,_Puerto_Rico" title="El Condado, Puerto Rico">Condado</a>.</p>\n<p>Places and monuments emphasized in tourism campaigns include: Old San Juan, promoting the historic nature of its colonial buildings and narrow streets covered by adoquine, a blue stone cast from furnace slag; they were brought over as ballast on Spanish ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> This includes the city\'s ancient defensive wall and forts, most notably <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">El Morro</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castillo_de_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Castillo de San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (Puerto Rico)">Castle of San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-5"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> On January 23, 1984 both of these edifices were catalogued as being part of humanity\'s cultural patrimony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-6"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> The restaurants and art galleries in the zone are visited by tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_57-7"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-57">[56]</a></sup> The local universities are promoted as historic places, most notably the campus of University of Puerto Rico located in R\xc3\xado Piedras, which is the oldest university on the island being founded in 1903.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_notable_residents_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of notable residents of San Juan, Puerto Rico">List of notable residents of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>San Juan is the birthplace of artists and musicians, locally known as <i>Sanjuaneros</i>, who have significantly influenced Puerto Rican culture. During the 20th century, the musical aspect of the city was influenced by performers including <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_Americans" title="West Indian Americans">Afro-Caribbean</a> dancer and choreographer <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_del_Villard" title="Sylvia del Villard">Sylvia del Villard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Enrique_Pedreira" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Enrique Pedreira">Jos\xc3\xa9 Enrique Pedreira</a> who became a composer of Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Puerto_Rico#Danza" title="Music of Puerto Rico">Danzas</a>. International musicians such as opera singer <a href="/wiki/Justino_D%C3%ADaz" title="Justino D\xc3\xadaz">Justino D\xc3\xadaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Daddy_Yankee" title="Daddy Yankee">Ram\xc3\xb3n Ayala</a> (Daddy Yankee) and <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a> were born in the city. Other notable residents include writers <a href="/wiki/Giannina_Braschi" title="Giannina Braschi">Giannina Braschi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Blanco_(writer)" title="Tom\xc3\xa1s Blanco (writer)">Tomas Blanco</a>, award-winning actors <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Juli%C3%A1" title="Ra\xc3\xbal Juli\xc3\xa1">Ra\xc3\xbal Juli\xc3\xa1</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benicio_del_Toro" title="Benicio del Toro">Benicio del Toro</a>, and comedian <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Agrelot" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Cordero_(educator)" title="Rafael Cordero (educator)">Rafael Cordero</a> (1790\xe2\x80\x931868), was influential in the development of Puerto Rican education and has been once renowned<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (August 2014)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> as " The Father of Public Education in Puerto Rico". The city is also the home of contemporary and classic art museums. The Puerto Rico Arts Museum owns the largest collection of contemporary art in Puerto Rico, housing over 1,100 permanent art pieces and displaying temporary exhibitions containing artwork from various locations through Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Museum_of_Contemporary_Art" title="Puerto Rico Museum of Contemporary Art">Puerto Rico Museum of Contemporary Art</a>, located in Santurce, specializes in contemporary artwork from Latin America and the Caribbean. The paintings displayed in the permanent exhibition are either acquired by the museum\'s administrative personnel or donated by artists and collectors. They are judged by a panel of painters, art critics, and scholars before being displayed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Other museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Casals" title="Pablo Casals">Pablo Casals</a> Museum, the Book Museum, Americas Museum and the National Gallery display historic items and artwork alongside contemporary art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> Miscellaneous museums such as the Children\'s Museum and the <a href="/wiki/Bacardi" title="Bacardi">Bacardi</a> Distillery (also known as the "Rum Cathedral") in nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a> appeal to different audiences through interactive exhibitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of San Juan, Puerto Rico">List of mayors of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>As one of Puerto Rico\'s 78 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipalities</a>, San Juan\'s government consists of two branches, the executive and the legislative. Those citizens eligible to vote directly elect a mayor and the municipal assembly for four-year terms. The municipal government is housed in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_City_Hall" title="San Juan City Hall">City Hall</a> or <i>Casa Alcaldia</i>, which is located at 153 San Francisco Street, facing the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Armas,_San_Juan" title="Plaza de Armas, San Juan">Plaza de Armas</a> at the center of <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alcald.C3.ADa_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alcald.C3.ADa-66">[65]</a></sup> City Hall was constructed based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrid,_Spain" title="Madrid, Spain">Madrid</a>\'s City Hall starting in 1604 and finally completed in 1789.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alcald.C3.ADa_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Alcald.C3.ADa-66">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The executive branch is headed by a popularly elected mayor. The office is currently held by <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Yul%C3%ADn_Cruz" title="Carmen Yul\xc3\xadn Cruz">Carmen Yul\xc3\xadn Cruz</a>, who was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2012" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2012">2012 general election</a>. Before her, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jorge_A._Santini" title="Jorge A. Santini">Jorge A. Santini</a> held the position for 12 years. In addition to running the city\'s day-to-day operations and supervising associated departments, the mayor is responsible for appointing a secretary-auditor and a treasurer. San Juan\'s Municipal Legislature is made up of 17 municipal legislators, elected at-large, which represent the city\'s population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asamblea_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asamblea-67">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<p>San Juan is also the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_I" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district I">Puerto Rico Senatorial district I</a>, which is represented by two Senators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Nadal_Power" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Nadal Power">Jos\xc3\xa9 Nadal Power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Luis_Nieves" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Nieves">Ram\xc3\xb3n Luis Nieves</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span></h3>\n<p>In 2010 there were 201 slayings in San Juan, a rate of around 50 per 100,000 residents. Law enforcement in San Juan is the joint responsibility of the Department of Police and Public Safety, also known as the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Police_Department" title="San Juan Police Department">San Juan Police Department</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police_Department" title="Puerto Rico Police Department">Puerto Rico Police Department</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> The Municipal Police, originally known as the "San Juan Municipal Guard", was created in 1521 and has active military and law enforcement functions, until 1980 when act #77 created municipal law enforcement agencies in Puerto Rico. It currently employs over 1,000 sworn officers plus civilian staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Media of Puerto Rico">Media of Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14"
