<small><i>(May 2017)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:189px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg/187px-Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg/281px-Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg/374px-Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg 2x" width="187"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMain tower of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> campus in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_Piedras" title="Rio Piedras">Rio Piedras</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>San Juan is home to many of Puerto Rico\'s institutions of higher learning. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UPRRP" title="UPRRP">University of Puerto Rico R\xc3\xado Piedras Campus</a> is located in San Juan, along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico,_Medical_Sciences_Campus" title="University of Puerto Rico, Medical Sciences Campus">University of Puerto Rico\'s Medical Sciences Campus</a>. Other colleges located in San Juan are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_the_Sacred_Heart_(Puerto_Rico)" title="University of the Sacred Heart (Puerto Rico)">University of the Sacred Heart</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Polytechnic University of Puerto Rico">Polytechnic University of Puerto Rico</a>, the Ana G. M\xc3\xa9ndez University System\'s <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_University_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Metropolitan University (Puerto Rico)">Metropolitan University</a>, the Metropolitan Campus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter_American_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Inter American University of Puerto Rico">Inter American University of Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Albizu_University" title="Carlos Albizu University">Carlos Albizu University</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelic_Seminary_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Evangelic Seminary of Puerto Rico">Evangelic Seminary of Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Advanced_Studies_on_Puerto_Rico_and_the_Caribbean" title="Center for Advanced Studies on Puerto Rico and the Caribbean">Center for Advanced Studies on Puerto Rico and the Caribbean</a>. There are smaller colleges located in the city, including the ICPR Junior College, the <i>Instituto de Banca y Comercio</i> and the International Junior College, located in Santurce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-college_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-college-72">[71]</a></sup> There are also several technical schools based in San Juan, including the Technological College of San Juan, the <i>Liceo de Artes y Ciencias</i>, Ramirez College of Business and Technology, and the Puerto Rico Technical Junior College. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Conservatory_of_Music" title="Puerto Rico Conservatory of Music">Puerto Rico Conservatory of Music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Escuela_de_Artes_Pl%C3%A1sticas_y_Dise%C3%B1o_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Escuela de Artes Pl\xc3\xa1sticas y Dise\xc3\xb1o de Puerto Rico">School of Fine Arts</a> in Old San Juan specialize in education that promotes the fine arts and music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-college_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-college-72">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_and_private_schools">Public and private schools</span></h3>\n<p>Also, San Juan is home to 136<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> public schools operated by the Puerto Rico Department of Education. Most of the specialized schools operated by the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico are located in San Juan. These schools emphasize topics such as Science and Math, Radio and Television, Arts, Trade, Music, and Sports, but also include other subjects such as Spanish, English, and Social Studies in their curriculum. In addition to dozens of state-run elementary, intermediate, and high schools, the government of the city of San Juan operates two bilingual schools, including one sports-magnet school, the first municipal-run schools in Puerto Rico.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Several private schools are located in San Juan, including Robinson and St. John\'s schools in the <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">Condado</a>, Perpetuo Socorro in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miramar,_Puerto_Rico" title="Miramar, Puerto Rico">Miramar</a>, St. John\'s Episcopal, Santa M\xc3\xb3nica and <a href="/wiki/Academia_San_Jorge" title="Academia San Jorge">Academia San Jorge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>, Commonwealth High School, La Merced and Esp\xc3\xadritu Santo in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a>, Escuela Josefita Monserrate de Selles, San Antonio, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colegio_San_Ignacio_de_Loyola" title="Colegio San Ignacio de Loyola">Colegio San Ignacio de Loyola</a>, San Jos\xc3\xa9 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cupeyville_School" title="Cupeyville School">Cupeyville</a>, St. Mary\'s, Boneville and Cupey Maria Montesory School in Cupey.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_San_Juan" title="Port of San Juan">Port of San Juan</a> is the fourth busiest seaport in the Western Hemisphere, ranked among the top 17 in the world in terms of container movement. It is also the largest home-based cruise port in the world with over a dozen cruise ships. It is the second busiest port in cruise volume after Miami.</p>\n<p>The Metropolitan Area is served by two airports. The <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a>, San Juan\'s primary commercial airport, is located eight miles (12.9\xc2\xa0km) from Old San Juan in the neighboring municipality of <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. The airport accommodates more than 30 domestic and international airlines and is the busiest airport in the Caribbean. It is often referred to as "The Gateway to the Caribbean" because it serves as the main connection to the island and the rest of the Caribbean for the United States and vice versa. The area\'s secondary airport is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fernando_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" title="Fernando Ribas Dominicci Airport">Fernando Ribas Dominicci Airport</a>, which is located directly across the San Antonio Creek or <i>Cano San Antonio</i> from Old San Juan in the Isla Grande district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> Dominicci Airport is used mainly by general aviation aircraft, charter flights, and some domestic commercial flights. It used to be the city\'s and also the island of Puerto Rico\'s main international gateway until the opening of Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Marin International Airport. It is now also widely used by the Isla Grande Flight School and Caribbean Flight Center, the only flight school on the island.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tren_Urbano" title="Tren Urbano">Tren Urbano</a></div>\n<p>At 4,300 vehicles per paved mile, San Juan has by far the highest density of vehicles on the road of any country in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> The city is served by five limited-access expressways and highways and numerous arterial avenues and boulevards, but continues to suffer from severe traffic congestion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Metropolitan_Bus_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Metropolitan Bus Authority">Metropolitan Bus Authority</a> (<i>Autoridad Metropolitana de Autobuses</i> or <i>AMA</i> in Spanish) provides daily bus transportation to residents of San Juan, Guaynabo, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Toa Baja, Trujillo Alto, Cata\xc3\xb1o and Carolina through 30 fixed routes. Its fleet consists of 277 regular buses and 35 handicap-accessible buses. AMA\'s ridership is estimated at 112,000 on weekdays.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> There is also a daily ferry service, known as the <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o_Ferry" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o Ferry">Cata\xc3\xb1o Ferry</a> (<i>La Lancha de Cata\xc3\xb1o</i>), which operates between Old San Juan and the town of <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="938" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif/220px-SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif/330px-SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif/440px-SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe T5, 21 and 53 buses pass between Old San Juan, Condado and Isla Verde. More information is available at <a class="external free" href="http://sjbus.info/" rel="nofollow">http://sjbus.info/</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In an attempt to decrease vehicle dependency and road congestion, the city built a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Tren_Urbano" title="Tren Urbano">Tren Urbano</a>" ("Urban Train"). The 10.7-mile (17.2\xc2\xa0km) line connects to 16\xc2\xa0stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> The project, which opened in late 2004, cost $2.25\xc2\xa0billion and was more than $1\xc2\xa0billion over budget and four years late. The Tren Urbano has received less ridership than was originally projected and has not significantly reduced the city\'s automobile traffic, despite a reported 7.5% ridership increase in 2006 over 2005. There is a planned project to build a "interurban light rail system" connecting the cities of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas_Rail" title="San Juan-Caguas Rail">San Juan and Caguas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Increased investment in public transportation, however, has not changed the fact that San Juan is an automobile-reliant city and its fast growth has sparked urban sprawl. As of mid-2010, the government has approved plans for a redesign of this Puerto Rican city, featuring a new mass transit system, new roads and intersections, and more beach-access points. No cars will be allowed inside the oldest part of city (Old San Juan). The plans hope to remedy previous poor urban planning in the oldest section of the city, the Isleta, while curbing reliance on motor vehicles. The plans for redevelopment also hope to make the city more appealing in order to attract new residents, as San Juan has suffered from a shrinking population over the past 60 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_utilities">Health and utilities</span></h2>\n<p>San Juan has an elaborate system of <a href="/wiki/Triage" title="Triage">triage</a>, hospital, and preventive care health services. The municipal government sponsors regular health fairs in different areas of the city focusing on health care for the elderly and the disabled. There are 20 hospitals in San Juan, half of them operated by the government. The largest hospital in San Juan and most important of Puerto Rico and the Caribbean<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> is the <b>Rio Piedras Medical Center</b>, or <i><b>Centro Medico de Rio Piedras</b></i> in Spanish. This hospital, founded in 1956, is operated by the Medical Services Administration of the Department of Health of Puerto Rico. It is made up of eight other hospitals.</p>\n<ul>\n<li>San Juan Municipal Hospital: This hospital is operated by the San Juan municipal government.</li>\n<li>Industrial Hospital: This is the hospital for Puerto Rico government employees, whether municipal or Commonwealth government employees. Normally, injured police officers and firefighters are cared for here.</li>\n<li>San Juan Pediatric Hospital - Also operated by the San Juan municipal government.</li>\n<li>Pediatric Hospital: Operated by the government of the Commonwealth, this is the main trauma hospital for pediatric cases.</li>\n<li>Centro Medico: This is the main hospital for trauma cases for Puerto Rico and the Caribbean.</li>\n<li>Centro Cardiovascular del Caribe (Caribbean Cardiovascular Center): This is the main hospital for open heart surgery in the Caribbean. It features a hotel for the patients\' families.</li>\n<li>Psychiatric Hospital: The main psychiatric hospital in Puerto Rico. Operated by the government of Puerto Rico.</li>\n<li>Psychiatric Correctional Hospital: It is both a hospital and correctional facility. It is operated jointly by the Puerto Rico Department of Corrections and the Medical Services Administration.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The city of San Juan operates 10 hospitals. Of these, nine are Diagnostic and Treatment Centers located in communities throughout San Juan. The main hospital is located at Centro Medico. These 10 hospitals are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Perla,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Perla, San Juan, Puerto Rico">La Perla</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_Puerto_Rico" title="Puerta de Tierra, Puerto Rico">Puerta de Tierra</a></li>\n<li>Llorens Torres</li>\n<li>Puerto Nuevo</li>\n<li>San Jos\xc3\xa9</li>\n<li>Rio Piedras</li>\n<li>Sabana Llana</li>\n<li>Hoare</li>\n<li>Santurce Parada 19</li>\n<li>General Hospital (Centro Medico)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Also, there are 10 private hospitals in San Juan. These are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Hospital Metropilitano</li>\n<li>Hospital Auxilio Mutuo</li>\n<li>Hospital Auxilio Mutuo Expreso</li>\n<li>Hospital de Veteranos: The main Veterans hospital in the Caribbean. Operated by the U.S. Veteran Healthcare System.</li>\n<li>Ashford Presbyterian Hospital</li>\n<li>Hospital Pavia Hato Rey</li>\n<li>Hospital Pavia Santurce</li>\n<li>San Jorge Children\'s Hospital: The most well known children\'s hospital in the San Juan Metropolitan Area.</li>\n<li>Hospital San Gerardo: Located at the Cupey neighborhood, is a small hospital but is also specialized in psychiatry and elderly.</li>\n<li>Hospital del Maestro (Teachers Hospital): Located in Hato Rey, this hospital is operated by the Puerto Rico Teachers Association.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1431" data-file-width="2237" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg/200px-Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg/300px-Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg/400px-Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA night view of the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Agrelot_Coliseum" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Teams based in San Juan have been notably successful in athletic competition. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santurce_Crabbers_(basketball)" title="Santurce Crabbers (basketball)">Santurce Crabbers</a> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Superior_Basketball_League" title="National Superior Basketball League">National Superior Basketball League</a> championship in 1998, 1999, 2000, 2001 and 2003 during this period being recognized as a dynasty. The San Juan Senators and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santurce_Crabbers_(baseball)" title="Santurce Crabbers (baseball)">Santurce Crabbers</a> were the two major baseball teams in the city, winning the championship of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Professional_Baseball_League" title="Puerto Rican Professional Baseball League">Puerto Rican Professional Baseball League</a> a total of seventeen times. The Santurce Crabbers are located third among teams with more championships in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a>, winning championships in the 1951, 1953, 1955, 1993 and 2000 editions of the tournament. The city has also been the host of events within the sports community; some examples include:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/1966_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="1966 Central American and Caribbean Games">1966 Central American and Caribbean Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/1979_Pan_American_Games" title="1979 Pan American Games">1979 Pan American Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Has been host of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_World_Series" title="Caribbean World Series">Caribbean World Series</a> nine times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> played 22 home games at <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a> in both 2003 and 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> The team also briefly considered moving permanently to San Juan before relocating to Washington, D.C.</li>\n<li>Hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2009 World Baseball Classic">2009</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2013 World Baseball Classic">2013 World Baseball Classic</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1974 FIBA World Championship">1974 FIBA World Championship</a> (basketball).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Has been host of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_Americas_Championship" title="FIBA Americas Championship">FIBA Americas Championship</a> five times (1980, 1993, 1999, 2003, 2009).</li>\n<li>The first edition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Entertainment</a>\'s pay per view <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Revolution" title="New Year\'s Revolution">New Year\'s Revolution</a> was held at the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Agrelot_Coliseum" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum</a> in January 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></li>\n<li>The Latin American Regional <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> in February 2010</li>\n<li>Host of Major League Baseball\'s 2010 "San Juan Series", three games of the Mets at Marlins held on June 28\xe2\x80\x9330, 2010 at <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The recently built $28 million San Juan Natatorium is beginning to attract islandwide and regional swim meets, as well winter training by top-rated mainland U.S. colleges and universities, including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">United States Military Academy</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Point" title="West Point">West Point</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annapolis" title="Annapolis">Annapolis</a>.</p>\n<p>In July 2007, the San Juan Golf Academy and its driving range began operating atop the city\'s former sanitary landfill in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Nuevo_(Hato_Rey)" title="Puerto Nuevo (Hato Rey)">Puerto Nuevo</a> and will eventually include the city\'s first and only 9-hole golf course.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline"
